<div id="review_1510785430" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1510785430" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388694025p2/3344685.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1510785430?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780356503967" href="/book/show/25895976-the-gathering-storm">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=books-i-own-kindle">books-i-own-kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1510785430" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7057800263400244197">Like a lot of fans of this series I was a little nervous going into <b>The Gathering Storm</b> because I wasn't sure if <b>Brandon Sanderson</b> would be able to capture the feel of the Wheel of Time series in quite the way <b>Robert Jordan</b> has created it. I'd never actually read a book by <b>Brandon Sanderson</b> before (although I'll certainly be buying some of them when I've finished this series!) so it wasn't a reflection on him as an author, just fears about a well loved series having a change in author. Of course</span>
  <span id="freeText7057800263400244197" style="display:none">Like a lot of fans of this series I was a little nervous going into <b>The Gathering Storm</b> because I wasn't sure if <b>Brandon Sanderson</b> would be able to capture the feel of the Wheel of Time series in quite the way <b>Robert Jordan</b> has created it. I'd never actually read a book by <b>Brandon Sanderson</b> before (although I'll certainly be buying some of them when I've finished this series!) so it wasn't a reflection on him as an author, just fears about a well loved series having a change in author. Of course I'm glad that <b>Robert Jordan</b> allowed someone else access to his notes so that the series wasn't left open ended but the nerves were definitely real when I picked up this book.<br /><br />Luckily that worry turned out to be unneeded though because this ended up being one of my favourite books in the series. Yes there are differences in the writing style between the two authors but overall I think the changes <b>Brandon Sanderson</b> made to some of the characters (and certainly the increased pacing of the story!) were for the better. The things that have irritated me more and more in the most recent books were markedly absent here and I enjoyed the book so much more because of that. It takes us back to the good old days when there was always something interesting happening, no more boring filler chapters and three thousand side characters being added in every instalment that had pretty much no relevant role in the overall storyline.<br /><br />The two characters who are really the main focus of <b>The Gathering Storm</b> are Rand and Egwene. Rand is on a difficult path and his storyline has been getting darker and darker as he tries to mold himself into someone who is capable of putting the greater good above the lives of individuals. It's completely against Rand's nature to allow people he considers under his protection, especially women, to get hurt in battle but he has come to the realisation that they won't be able to win at Tarmon Gai'don without casualties. It's quite sad to see Rand fighting against his instincts and also struggling with his madness in this book but his storyline is definitely interesting and I think he made a key realisation towards the end of the book that is going to make things a little easier for him going forwards.<br /><br />Egwene really shines in this book, she really started to show her strength in the previous instalment and that just continues here. She has grown so much since she was raised as the Amyrlin Seat of the rebel Aes Sedai and her wisdom and cunning shine through in this book. There is no doubt in my mind that she is going to make a fantastic Amyrlin and I can't wait to watch her bring all the ajas back together again under the white tower where they all belong. It's going to be an exciting time for the Aes Sedai and I'm particularly interested to see how they deal with the Seanchan after the betrayal in this book.<br /><br />It's obvious that various plot threads are being woven closer together now that the end of the series is approaching. I can't actually believe there are only two books left but I am more excited about this series than ever and I can't wait to see how each of the character's stories end.<br /><br />__________________________<br /><br />Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/17825167-the-gathering-storm&gt;Buddies, Books &amp; Baubles&lt;/a&gt; starting &lt;b&gt;1st December 2016&lt;/b&gt;" rel="nofollow noopener"></a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7057800263400244197" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_82759754" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/82759754" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/82759754?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82759754" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11965603382413046362">Okay, I've got to put everything else aside till I read this...it's nearly 800 pages and other people at the library are waiting for me to finish it.<br/><br/>Well at least they finally killed *** ******. Yeah, I won't put in a spoiler, not that it would matter that much, but then Sanderson has continued Jordan's established pattern of actually tying up few plot points per volume. That is I suppose why it will (he says) take 2 more of these gargantuan tomes to complete this story. <br/><br/>Okay (I seem to say that</span>
  <span id="freeText11965603382413046362" style="display:none">Okay, I've got to put everything else aside till I read this...it's nearly 800 pages and other people at the library are waiting for me to finish it.<br /><br />Well at least they finally killed *** ******. Yeah, I won't put in a spoiler, not that it would matter that much, but then Sanderson has continued Jordan's established pattern of actually tying up few plot points per volume. That is I suppose why it will (he says) take 2 more of these gargantuan tomes to complete this story. <br /><br />Okay (I seem to say that a lot), once I got into this my first reaction to the rambling narration was I just don't care anymore. But in a way I do care. The farther I got into this "thing" the more the overpowering feeling of sadness at what could have been overwhelmed me. I can't pick up one of these books without getting angry and frustrated. As has been pointed out before, this was originally planned as a seven (that's 7) book series...somehow it has bloated up to 12 volumes with 2 more to come. <br /><br />Let me say that the first 6 volumes of this series (by Robert Jordan) are some of the best writing I have ever come in contact with. This stood to be (I believe) one of the great fantasy series (and possibly great fiction works) of all time. But, for some reason (and all I can do is speculate what it was as the author did not tell us) it was turned into a rambling soap opera. I live in hope that some one in a future generation will take the entire 14 volumes (plus the prequel New Spring) and turn them over to a good editor.<br /><br />I know some of Mr. Jordan's fans are not happy with me here, I have seen the "5 star ratings" and believe me when I say I'm happy for you. I know that there are those of you who love the repetitive conversations, the accounts of the same events from several different people, the endless and pointless war of the sexes. The plot point where Nynaeve runs to Cadsuane probably thrilled you. And you probably "felt" that "the one she sent" to talk to Rand, and Rand's reaction are "very important". Okay... good. It took long enough to get there and what did we accomplish? Well, Rand ******* again.<br /><br />Actually I really mean it, I'm glad you are enjoying this.<br /><br />I'm not. <br /><br />I believe I've made my opinion of this volume and the series in general plain here. I know that a lot of you will disagree with me and some will point out that the books sell in huge numbers.<br /><br />The same can be said of Harlequin Romances.<br /><br />I have always wondered if the fact that the books were all "best sellers" may not have been their downfall. I always wondered (wonder) if "somebody" might not have said to Mr. Jordan, "hey this thing is making tons of money, why wind it up at seven volumes?" Of course as I said, no one can be sure of something like that. All we know is that like Frankenstein's monster this story just keeps stumbling along.<br /><br />I don't think I'll take the next two out of the library as soon as they're published. If I finish the "series" I may just wait till the last volume is finished and read it then. Maybe I'll even take time to reread the first volumes a second time once the thing is finished. The first ones (first 5 or 6) were really good even excellent. As I said, what might have been. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11965603382413046362" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_362649768" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/362649768" />
    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10743961-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422270416p2/10743961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/362649768?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/10743961-rob">Rob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/12743267-the-gathering-storm">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-before-goodreads">read-before-goodreads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=author-male">author-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=not-a-bookclub-club">not-a-bookclub-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=wheel-of-time">wheel-of-time</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer362649768" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6622728191643178737"><b>Executive Summary:</b> By comparison to the previous books, this book moves at breakneck speed. It remains one of my favorite of the series, but isn't quite as good as I remember it being. I do think that Brandon Sanderson does an excellent job and picking up where Mr. Jordan left off however.<br/> <br/><b>Audiobook:</b> Another fantastic performance by both Michael Kramer and Kate Reading. They really bring these characters to life, and I can't see myself ever picking up my paperback copies again when I could liste</span>
  <span id="freeText6622728191643178737" style="display:none"><b>Executive Summary:</b> By comparison to the previous books, this book moves at breakneck speed. It remains one of my favorite of the series, but isn't quite as good as I remember it being. I do think that Brandon Sanderson does an excellent job and picking up where Mr. Jordan left off however.<br /> <br /><b>Audiobook:</b> Another fantastic performance by both Michael Kramer and Kate Reading. They really bring these characters to life, and I can't see myself ever picking up my paperback copies again when I could listen to the audio instead.<br /> <br /><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br />When I finally got into the Wheel of Time, this book had just come out. By the time I caught up, it was out in paperback but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8253920.Towers_of_Midnight__Wheel_of_Time___13_" title="Towers of Midnight (Wheel of Time, #13) by Robert Jordan" rel="nofollow noopener">Towers of Midnight</a> hadn't been released yet. So this is where I had to join the fans in waiting for an end. Hardly a comparison to fans who have been reading this series since the beginning.<br /><br />This is the book that turned me into a rabid Brandon Sanderson fan, and I proceeded to consume nearly every book he had written to this point. I feel that Mr. Jordan had finally returned to form with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13888.Knife_of_Dreams__Wheel_of_Time___11_" title="Knife of Dreams (Wheel of Time, #11) by Robert Jordan" rel="nofollow noopener">Knife of Dreams</a>, so it's not much of a surprise that this book moves at a much faster pace than some of the previous ones.<br /><br />For me the clear star of the book is Egwene. At first glance it might be easy to give Mr. Sanderson credit for making her into an awesome character, but in my opinion this book is simply the fulfillment of path Mr. Jordan setup in the last few novels of the series. Her chapters were always by far the most interesting parts, even over my those of my favorite character Mat's chapters.<br /><br />I remember reading a lot of criticism from fans that Mr. Sanderson didn't do a good job with Mat, and that he changed a lot from the way Mr. Jordan wrote him. During my first reading of the series I didn't agree. After a second reading however, I am inclined to agree somewhat. Mat did feel a bit off. I almost want to say a bit "goofy" compared to the previous few books. However, I still enjoyed his parts quite a lot, and I'm definitely looking forward to what I know is yet to come for him in the final two books.<br /><br />I don't remember being so annoyed at Rand this late in the series as I was during this reread. I think that's part of why I didn't enjoy this book quite as much as I remember. I don't put that on Mr. Sanderson however. <br /><br />Much like Perrin (who annoyed me even more even though his part is quite small), Rand is at a point in his story to be very unlikable. Mr. Sanderson must write the characters forward to their conclusion in a way that follows with everything that's going on.<br /><br />Both are dealing with a lot of baggage. I think I just have less tolerance for it than I did during my first read. Especially after how great Egwene (and to a lesser degree Nynaeve's parts) are. <br /><br />Overall things are finally moving towards a resolution, and even though I know what's coming I can't wait to read it all again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6622728191643178737" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1556291467" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1556291467" />
    <a title="Emerson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38007906-emerson"><img alt="Emerson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589992055p2/38007906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1556291467?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emerson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emerson" href="/user/show/38007906-emerson">Emerson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11203972-the-gathering-storm">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38007906-emerson?shelf=lidos-em-2016">lidos-em-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1556291467" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8701336496807945580">"Two hands. One to destroy, the other to save. Which had he lost?"<br/><br/>Excelente. Estou muito impressionado com a qualidade desse livro. A narrativa sutil do Brandon Sanderson deu a acelerada que a série precisava. Não senti mudanças na personalidade dos personagens, e isso me agradou muito, era algo que eu receava...<br/>Muitos momentos tensos e agoniantes me fizeram ter diferentes sensações, da alegria a tristeza...<br/>Simplesmente fantástico.<br/><br/>"At the end of time, <br/>when the many become one, <br/>the last storm sha</span>
  <span id="freeText8701336496807945580" style="display:none">"Two hands. One to destroy, the other to save. Which had he lost?"<br /><br />Excelente. Estou muito impressionado com a qualidade desse livro. A narrativa sutil do Brandon Sanderson deu a acelerada que a série precisava. Não senti mudanças na personalidade dos personagens, e isso me agradou muito, era algo que eu receava...<br />Muitos momentos tensos e agoniantes me fizeram ter diferentes sensações, da alegria a tristeza...<br />Simplesmente fantástico.<br /><br />"At the end of time, <br />when the many become one, <br />the last storm shall gather its angry winds<br /> to destroy a land already dying. <br />And at its center,<br />the blind man shall stand upon his own grave. <br />There he shall see again, <br />and weep for what has been wrought."</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12514783695105653476">To be real honest, I actually think this is the best book of the series so far. Brandon Sanderson is a much better writer than Robert Jordan, and mind you I read all 11 books by Jordan so he's not THAT shabby! Harriet (Robert jordan's widow) picked the PERFECT writer to finish the series from Jordan's notes. He grew up with those books and is a huge fan boy of the series so he is ever so mindful to stay within the parameters of the world and the previous books in the series. He's paid a great de</span>
  <span id="freeText12514783695105653476" style="display:none">To be real honest, I actually think this is the best book of the series so far. Brandon Sanderson is a much better writer than Robert Jordan, and mind you I read all 11 books by Jordan so he's not THAT shabby! Harriet (Robert jordan's widow) picked the PERFECT writer to finish the series from Jordan's notes. He grew up with those books and is a huge fan boy of the series so he is ever so mindful to stay within the parameters of the world and the previous books in the series. He's paid a great deal of attention to be factually correct and to write more in Jordan's style than his own. But an alert reader who has also read Sanderson's work will see his style peek through from time to time.<br /><br />I really like the whole series but I'm overly fond of 1,000 plus page books. It's a huge commitment to take this series on now, but one I still feel is worth the commitment. I think it will always be known as one of the great epic fantasies of all time.<br /><br />I'll add more once I've finished!</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780356503967" href="/book/show/25895976-the-gathering-storm">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer7215530486694167160">Amazing! There are too many great things to keep track of and mention in reviews about <i>WoT</i> books at this point but, in general, all you have to really know is that it was amazing. It definitely felt weird at the beginning to have Brandon Sanderson writing. Yes, I could tell! The 30 page prologue gave it away. Oh how I do not miss Jordan's never-ending prologues.<br/><br/>Scary Rand is brilliant. I loved Rand in this installment, damn. But I'm glad that despite the 'heaviness' and 'finality' of it all that</span>
  <span id="freeText7215530486694167160" style="display:none">Amazing! There are too many great things to keep track of and mention in reviews about <i>WoT</i> books at this point but, in general, all you have to really know is that it was amazing. It definitely felt weird at the beginning to have Brandon Sanderson writing. Yes, I could tell! The 30 page prologue gave it away. Oh how I do not miss Jordan's never-ending prologues.<br /><br />Scary Rand is brilliant. I loved Rand in this installment, damn. But I'm glad that despite the 'heaviness' and 'finality' of it all that the humour in these books is still sharp and witty and fantastic. Really glad that none of that was lost when Sanderson took over. And I've GOT to mention Egwene. EGWENE! Egwene slowly taking over The White Tower from the inside was one of the most engaging things to read DAMN. Can't wait for everything that's been predicted and promised and foreshadowed to happen in the final final books. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_206042259" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/206042259" />
    <a title="Eric Allen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6229358-eric-allen"><img alt="Eric Allen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560117879p2/6229358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/206042259?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eric Allen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eric Allen" href="/user/show/6229358-eric-allen">Eric Allen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer206042259" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16044796016582359826">The Gathering Storm<br/>Book 12 of the Wheel of time<br/>By Robert Jordan and Brandon Sanderson<br/><br/>A Wheel of Time Retrospective by Eric Allen<br/><br/>In 1990 Robert Jordan published The Eye of the World and changed my life forever. At that time the series was to be a trilogy. Ten books, a prequel of significant size, and a companion guide later he died with the story unfinished and three volumes of the series left to be written by another writer from extensive notes, partially written scenes and extensive dictations </span>
  <span id="freeText16044796016582359826" style="display:none">The Gathering Storm<br />Book 12 of the Wheel of time<br />By Robert Jordan and Brandon Sanderson<br /><br />A Wheel of Time Retrospective by Eric Allen<br /><br />In 1990 Robert Jordan published The Eye of the World and changed my life forever. At that time the series was to be a trilogy. Ten books, a prequel of significant size, and a companion guide later he died with the story unfinished and three volumes of the series left to be written by another writer from extensive notes, partially written scenes and extensive dictations that he gave during the final weeks of his life. Honestly, I'm touched that he cared enough about his fans that he spent so much of his remaining time on this Earth making sure that the groundwork was firmly set for another author to take the helm and finish the series. The writer chosen to complete the final volumes of The Wheel of Time was Brandon Sanderson. At the beginning, Tor wanted him to simply slap together an ending and have it out by the end of the year. Sanderson, a HUGE and longtime fan of the series, and Jordan's widow Harriet MacDougal, had to practically fight to get these final volumes finished in a way that Jordan himself would be proud of. But, luckily, Tor did eventually come around and see that their way was for the best. As he began writing, Sanderson found that the book was going to be nearly three times the length of the longest book in the series to date, and the fans were beginning to get restless, five years having passed since <a href="www.goodreads.com/review/show/214162455" rel="nofollow noopener"> Knife of Dreams</a>, the previous volume, had been released. So, Sanderson and Harriet set to work splitting the final volume into three. This is all explained in the forward by Sanderson in far better detail than I'm giving here if you care to read it. This meant that a new volume to the series could be published almost immediately to sate the fans whilst the rest of the story was worked out and written. The fruit of all that dealing, cutting, splitting, and reworking of the plot was The Gathering Storm.<br /> <br />The Wheel of Time is a series that, for me, started out as the best thing I’d ever read before in my life, but by the time it got to the sixth volume had grown overly long, somewhat boring, and stagnant. The last three volumes to be released in the series have made up for the several before them, in my opinion, by finally bringing some much needed resolution and action back to the series. Looking back on the story, those slow and boring books were needed parts of the whole, it just so happened that all of the boring happened to occur at the same time in the storyline and made for some very dull books in the middle.<br /> <br />Jordan pulled the series out of it’s rut with Knife of Dreams, the final volume he completed before his death, and promised that the end was nigh, with a single volume left to be written. Reading his blog posts about this final volume it was clear that he knew he was running out of time, and he wanted desperately to get the series finished in one final go before he died, but, unfortunately he was unable to. The world lost a brilliant storyteller, and, by many accounts, a great man on that day. <br /> <br />As the storm of the Last Battle gathers over the world, Rand finds himself desperate to make peace with the Seanchan, and bring peace and stability back to the land of Arad Doman, where he believes one of the Forsaken has taken up residence, sowing chaos and destruction. Meanwhile, captive by the usurper Amyrlin Seat Elaida within the White Tower, Egwene works to bring the crumbling order of the Aes Sedai back together so that they might stand with the Dragon Reborn at the Last Battle. The story mostly revolves around these two characters as they struggle with the destinies placed upon them, being dragged lower and lower into the depths of darkness and despair.<br /><br />Through constant beatings, a refusal to bend under Elaida, and wisdom far beyond her years Egwene manages to gain the respect of powerful Aes Sedai within the White Tower, working to mend the rifts between women who should be working together rather than showing open hostility toward one another. Slowly, and painstakingly she works to repair the damage that the Forsaken and the Black Ajah have done to the Tower, finally coming to realize what it truly means to be the Amyrlin Seat and an Aes Sedai of the White Tower.<br /><br />Rand has been broken, and beaten, and bloodied, and tortured, and maimed. He is haunted by the voice of a dead madman, and feels the weight of his duty as the savior of the world pressing down hard upon him. He has come to realize that he need not survive the Last Battle so long as he wins it, and has put everything he has into it. He sets aside love, honor and decency, willing to do anything it takes just to win, sinking deeper and deeper into darkness and insanity, using himself up with no thought of leaving anything behind after all is said and done. Cadsuane desperately works to teach him how to laugh again, but her efforts seem completely ineffective. When finally faced with what he has become, Rand runs to the peak of Dragonmount to find who he truly is and the reasons why he fights.<br /><br />The good? As Wheel of Time books go, this is one of the best, and as a follow up to Knife of Dreams, it was all WoT fans could have asked for and more. It has everything we loved about the first half of the series in it, with very little of the bad from the middle volumes that gummed up the works and slowed the plot to a crawl. I really enjoyed how the story narrowed down and focused on the struggles of these two characters. Some of the best books in the series have been the ones that focus on a smaller group of the characters rather than taking a broader view of the story. The way that they are both brought down as far as they can be brought and then finally find their redemption is very powerful. The character development is extremely good. You can really see how far these characters have come since the beginning of the series, and also, how much they are still the same. And it’s not just Rand and Egwene, other main characters that have been relegated to secondary roles in this book show how they’ve grown since the beginning as well. Nyneave, Siuan, Min, and many others to name a few.<br /><br />The scene at the end where Rand overcomes everything is probably one of the most beautiful moments in the entire series, especially with how long it’s been coming. Every book sees him lose a little more, be brought a little lower, be broken a little further. To have him finally overcome it all, and in such a powerful and beautifully written way was well worth the wait and many troubles that this book saw in finally making it to publication.<br /><br />The bad? Mat, my favorite character in the series, seemed a bit over the top and out of character. Oh, the parts with him were completely hilarious, I’ll give you that, but he wasn’t himself. He felt a bit off, like Sanderson was trying too hard to get his personality right and exaggerated his more notable traits a little too much. Thankfully this problem was mostly corrected in the next volume. And I do completely understand. This is not Brandon Sanderson’s book. He’s only finishing it. He was not the one that made these characters and he’s doing his best, and working very hard at it to make these books as good as they can possibly be.<br /><br />There are a lot of small errors that only the most avid of Wheel of Time fans will notice, details that are a bit off, characters not where they’re supposed to be, a few misspelled names, things of that nature. Though completely understandable under the circumstances, they’re still noticeable to anyone who has read the series as many times as I have.<br /><br />The ugly? Gawyn. To put it bluntly there are only two characters in this series that are bigger retards than he is, his sister and his mother. The amount of the story devoted to him and his stupidity was highly annoying to me. He’s been nothing but an oath-breaking, murdering tool that has shunned his duties, his family, his nation, and a hundred other things, to ride around on his horse and wave his sword around for attention so everyone around him knows how big his dick is. The only consolation is the constant ripping that Gareth Bryne does on him, never letting him forget that he’s broken his oaths, been a complete moron, and shunned his true duties for far too long. That Robert Jordan ever thought anyone could ever feel any sympathy for this idiot boggles the mind. You have this beautifully crafted, laid out, and written story with Rand and Egwene and through it all you keep getting interruptions with this jackass as if he thinks he’s important to the overall plot or something. He does do one or two important things in other books, I will give you that, but most of those are through stupidity that only made things worse for both sides, or things that easily could have been done by an unnamed bit player. In this book, he’s out of place, and breaks into the parts that I was really interested in far too often.<br /><br />Aviendha, one of my favorite characters in the series, keeps thinking to herself that she needs to be more like Elayne, my absolute least favorite character in the series. This was very hard to stomach. She’s better than that. She’s strong, stubborn and learns from every mistake that she makes. Elayne, on the other hand is weak, stupid, and hasn’t made a single millimeter of character development since the series began. To have Aviendha constantly thinking that she needs to be more like the character I typically skip any and all chapters about because the utter douchebaggery and stupidity of Elayne make my head hurt just trying to fathom seemed very wrong to me.<br /><br />After all of the rushing, the cutting, the rewriting, the splitting, and hasty editing, The Gathering Storm was still an extremely good book. In fact, I think that in the face of everything that stood in the way of this book's publication, it’s a miracle that it turned out half as well as it did. I loved this book. It has become my second favorite in the series right behind The Shadow Rising because of how well written and paced it is, and how beautifully sweet and long awaited the events at the end were. Though there are a few small errors that are perfectly understandable in the circumstances, this book is probably one of the best books I’ve ever read for Rand’s storyline alone. Brandon Sanderson has done an extremely good job at getting inside Robert Jordan’s head, and other than the few small things I mentioned, I couldn’t tell any difference in the tone or writing style between the two writers. <br /><br />I’m giving this book 5 stars. That the things I mentioned here were the only flaws that I could find in the entire book only speaks to how great a writer Brandon Sanderson is. That he was able to write something this good, and this beautiful with what he was given, while also writing a book of his own, and fighting to get enough time to write a book that Robert Jordan could be proud of is completely amazing to me. A few small errors can certainly be overlooked in the face of that. He deserves a perfect score for this book. He was given an impossible task and he’s exceeded all my expectations in the two out of three books that he’s completed and I eagerly await the final volume. He was definitely the right man for the job of completing Robert Jordan’s masterpiece. This is a book that I think Robert Jordan would smile on.<br /> <br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/list/6229358?shelf=read" rel="nofollow noopener"> Check out my other reviews.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16044796016582359826" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1367467233" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1367467233" />
    <a title="JDR" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24299015-jdr"><img alt="JDR" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593909092p2/24299015.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1367467233?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="JDR" class="user" itemprop="url" name="JDR" href="/user/show/24299015-jdr">JDR</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780765341532" href="/book/show/7141427-the-gathering-storm">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1367467233" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1323043258346669804">The fact that I am rewriting this review is a testament to the greatness that the Wheel of Time can present to me.<br/><br/>Obviously, you can see the rating, but you may not know that those 5-star ratings are rarer than you can imagine for me to give. Once GR gives the ability to half-stars, my ratings are gonna grow that much more rarer. But anyways, why do I love the Gathering Storm? You will definitely find out.<br/><br/><b> Sanderson's Writing. </b> I do not know any person who has actually read this series who could</span>
  <span id="freeText1323043258346669804" style="display:none">The fact that I am rewriting this review is a testament to the greatness that the Wheel of Time can present to me.<br /><br />Obviously, you can see the rating, but you may not know that those 5-star ratings are rarer than you can imagine for me to give. Once GR gives the ability to half-stars, my ratings are gonna grow that much more rarer. But anyways, why do I love the Gathering Storm? You will definitely find out.<br /><br /><b> Sanderson's Writing. </b> I do not know any person who has actually read this series who couldn't immediately tell that this was a different individual writing the story. In a way, it was a good thing that out of all the books that Sanderson had to jump in and write, it would be the climax. Because Sanderson couldn't have built the intricate world that RJ had created, at least not then. RJ crafted the world and something that Sanderson excels at is pacing because those battles scenes and confrontations were heart-pumping. Now that we had a developed world, we could go ahead and make it explode. <br /><br /><b> 2. Gawyn. </b> I do not need to describe the stupidity and just WTF sort of crap that he makes you react to when I can just show you evidence like this: <br /><br /><i> Lelaine wasn't beautiful, but she was pretty, particularly when she smiled. Slender and graceful, without a speck of gray in her <br />dark hair, an almond face with full lips. She looked up at him with eyes that were far too comely to belong to a woman of her <br />craftiness. And she seemed to know. She understood that she was just attractive enough to draw attention, but not stunning <br />enough to make men wary. <br />She was a woman of the most dangerous type. One who felt real, who made men think they might be able to hold her attention. <br />She wasn't pretty like Egwene, who made you want to spend time with her. This woman's smile made you want to count the <br />knives on your belt and in your boot, just to make sure none of them had found their way into your back while you were <br />distracted. <br /></i><br /><br /><b> 3. Perrin? Perrin who? </b><br /><br /><b> 4. Controversial Mat. </b> Why is there so much controversy with Mat? Is it because he doesn't really sound like he is supposed? You know, I laughed a lot with this Mat and everything. We had action scenes, typical aes sedai confrontations, some Aludra hints. Yet, the tie-breaker is that Mat lacked the charm. He was too serious and that's why its hard to be fond of him in the same way. Especially when he breaks the record for longest "Women are so complicated, I don't get them" speech. <br /><br />Now, let us get on to the real meat. Egwene and Rand, first with Egwene.<br /><br /><i> She was the cause of the <br />problems in the White Tower, she was the one who caused division between rebels and loyalists. She had taken Rand captive <br />and beaten him. She was a disaster! </i><br /><br /><b> 5. Egwene. </b> OMG THE FIRST REAL CONCLUSION TO A MAJOR STORYLINE!!! It<br />was pretty epic seeing Egwene face off the Elaida and the Seanchan! Like really, what does a woman have to do to be Amyrlin Seat around here? Although if Elaida and Egwene were running during a presidential election, Egwene would obviously have the best campaign.<br /><br /><i> "Can't you see it?" Egwene asked. "Don't you feel the pain? The agony of watching the Tower crumble around you? Could any <br />beating compare to that?" </i><br /><br />Also, she says that to Silviarin, the red ajah Mistress of Novices who also becomes the Keeper of the Chronicles because a) she should be and b) Its a brilliant political move to reestablish bonds with the Red ajah. It was interesting to see the relationship between Silviarin and Egwene progress, seeing each of them learn more about the other until eventually they garner a mutual respect for one another. Silviarin is the only one who stands up for Egwene and against Elaida! <br /><br />On the subject of an individual's character, the Siuan x Gareth ship has sailed, Bon Voyage! The one quote that i did want to mention was the one where Siuan mentions how Gareth will praise you with the same gratitude whether you are a servant or a soldier. That made me think on the Harry Potter quote of how you can tell a person's character by the way he treats his inferiors and he treats them with respect and honest gratitude. Go Bryne! <br /><br />Also, indirectly Racist Egwene quote:<br /><br /><i> "Siuan was deposed by the bare minimum number of Sitter required," Egwene said. "One of them was Black, making her vote <br />invalid. </i><br /><br />Damn.<br /><br />Now, the Battle of the White Tower aka "THE MOST EPIC BATTLE SINCE FALME LIKE WHAT THE SHIT IS THIS SLICE OF GOODNESS!" which had been following Verin's literally mimd-blowing revelation that she was Black...Ajah. I knew that but I didn't expect her to also help Egwene and give her the best solution to the problem of "Who is Black Ajah? Is it you or is it you? IDK!" Verin is the MVP.<br /><br />Then, the Battle scene. I swear if this isn't the concrete example of why world-building is so important, its like I was right there. In my mind, it was a mix of itself and the Two Towers LoTR (on a completely different note, the four core LoTR arrive in the mail today for me! So excited!). I saw serpents flying in the sky attacking Aes Sedai and Egwene fighting back. Honestly, I was kinda of imagining Egwene in the same light as Daenarys from A Song of Ice and Fire, except the dragons. Just the most badass female character like woah!! BADASS WOMAN ARE COOL.<br /><br /><i> "That's what I am," Rand said. "A story. A legend. To be told to children years from now, spoken of in whispers." He shook his <br />head. "Sometimes, you can't turn back. You have to keep pressing on. And sometimes, you know this climb is your last. <br />"You all claim that I have grown too hard, that I will inevitably shatter and break if I continue on. But you assume that there <br />needs to be something left of me to continue on. That I need to climb back down the mountain once I've reached the top. <br />"That's the key, Nynaeve. I see it now. I will not live through this, and so I don't need to worry about what might happen to me <br />after the Last Battle. I don't need to hold back, don't need to salvage anything of this beaten up soul of mine. I know that I must <br />die. Those who wish for me to be softer, willing to bend, are those who cannot accept what will happen to me." He looked down <br />at Min again. Many times before, Nynaeve had seen affection in his eyes when he regarded her, but this time they were blank. <br />Set in that same, emotionless face. <br />"We can find a way, Rand," Nynaeve said. "Surely there is a way to win but also let you live." <br />"No," he growled softly. "Do not tempt me down that path again. It only leads to pain, Nynaeve. I ... I used to think about <br />leaving something behind to help the world survive once I died, but that was a struggle to keep living. I can't indulge myself. I'll <br />climb this bloody mountain and face the sun. You all will deal with what comes next. That is how it must be." <br />She opened her mouth to object again, but he gave her a sharp glance. "That is how it must be, Nynaeve." </i><br /><br /><b> 6. Rand. </b> Rand is such a special character to me because he is the closest representation of the MC of the epic fantasy that I am writing. RJ and I are really alile on that front when it comes to the struggles thay a person in that position would deal with and how they would respond.<br /><br />This Rand is not necessarily Evil but he is umbelievably cold. I just read the first chapter of freakin Zen Rand, but at this point, Rand was so dark that he was actually terrifying. He was straying from the hero's path so hard.<br /><br />The way he went about in trying to destroy Graendal was unbelievable. He was literally about to nuclear bomb them, I mean that is what Balefire is pretty much! Except worse because it erases them completely from existence. <br /><br />The climax with Tam and his own inner struggle was what elavated this from a 4star to a 5-star. <br /><br />The entirety if Chapter 47-50. I wish i could just copy the entire chapters onto here, but there just isn't enough space because honestly, I can't just quote a specific lart because ALL of it is gold and all of it adds on top of what came before it. Chapter 50 was the best shit from Rand I have seen since the battle in the sky in the Great Hunt. This was however, a very philosophical climax.<br /><br />Also, I LOVE how Lews Therin has not been confirmed yet. To me, he is a metaphor at this point and you can take the statement where Rand says he wont hear his voice again in many directions.<br /><br />In conclusion, bravo everything. But especially Rand. He is the reason why I love this series as much as I do and thank Sanderson for his beautiful execution and RJ for crafting every piece of the world and characters.<br /><br />+ Rand Al'Thor<br />+ Egwne Al'Veara<br />+ Battle of the White Tower<br />+ Philosophical Climax<br /> <br />BUY/SKIP/RENT: BUY<br />Final Score: 9.0 / 10<br /><br />Favorite Books from #1 to last<br /><i> The Gathering Storm<br />The Great Hunt <br />The Fires of Heaven <br />The Eye of the World<br />Knife of Dreams<br />The Shadow Rising<br />The Path of Daggers<br />New Spring<br />A Crown of Swords<br />Lord of Chaos<br />The Dragon Reborn<br />Winter's Heart<br />Crossroads of Twilight </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1323043258346669804" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780356503967" href="/book/show/25895976-the-gathering-storm">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34286188-shobhit-sharad?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34286188-shobhit-sharad?shelf=robert-jordan">robert-jordan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34286188-shobhit-sharad?shelf=brandon-sanderson">brandon-sanderson</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1707435051" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10435439016085465379">"The Wheel weaves as the Wheel wills."<br/><br/>And it wove the best it could for this series. Brandon Sanderson writing the last few books is a definite gain for the Wheel of Time. <br/><br/>Though this world belongs to Jordan, it <i>needed</i> Sanderson, for the pace of the story, for the added humor which is not just funny to the Aiel. <br/><br/>Because by now, I really know what Seanchan armour looks like, I know what Choeden Kal is, and I don't want to be reminded about the appearances of every fricking person. All of this was</span>
  <span id="freeText10435439016085465379" style="display:none">"The Wheel weaves as the Wheel wills."<br /><br />And it wove the best it could for this series. Brandon Sanderson writing the last few books is a definite gain for the Wheel of Time. <br /><br />Though this world belongs to Jordan, it <i>needed</i> Sanderson, for the pace of the story, for the added humor which is not just funny to the Aiel. <br /><br />Because by now, I really know what Seanchan armour looks like, I know what Choeden Kal is, and I don't want to be reminded about the appearances of every fricking person. All of this was acceptable up to a point. But now that we are approaching the end of all things, I would like the stories to converge and conclude. And that did happen, thank you Mr. Sanderson.<br /><br />Though there was a slight change in the writing-style, it was much close to the way Mr. Jordan wrote. Rand was certainly pitiful, though there is yet hope for him. A plus point was, for me, the absence of Elayne. There was too much of her in the previous few books. Egwene, no doubt, the star of the book, won over my heart. </span>

<div id="review_1686767710" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1686767710" />
    <a title="Trent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19885276-trent"><img alt="Trent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601477767p2/19885276.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1686767710?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trent" href="/user/show/19885276-trent">Trent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19885276-trent?shelf=wheel-of-time">wheel-of-time</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1686767710" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4051541236681355495">The first thing you should know about me is that I'm one of the weird people who discovered the Wheel of Time because I was already a fan of Brandon Sanderson, and not the reverse (unlike the majority of readers). Mistborn was one the first Fantasy series I ever read, and it's one of the reasons I'm such a fan of the genre to this day. It's also why I cracked open the Eye of the World on summer vacation way back in 2012.<br/><br/>So, in a sense, the last few years have been leading to me reading this firs</span>
  <span id="freeText4051541236681355495" style="display:none">The first thing you should know about me is that I'm one of the weird people who discovered the Wheel of Time because I was already a fan of Brandon Sanderson, and not the reverse (unlike the majority of readers). Mistborn was one the first Fantasy series I ever read, and it's one of the reasons I'm such a fan of the genre to this day. It's also why I cracked open the Eye of the World on summer vacation way back in 2012.<br /><br />So, in a sense, the last few years have been leading to me reading this first Sanderson-penned Wheel of Time book. A lot has changed - I've read many other authors (some of which I actually like better than Sanderson), but I was still very excited to start this book.<br /><br />First, though, I have to give credit where it is due - to the Creator, Robert Jordan. In my opinion, he is the best world-builder in modern Fantasy, and maybe even in all of modern Fiction. I adore the world of the Wheel of Time. The cultures, the prophecies, the magic system, the history, the map (it's an important detail, okay?) - are just the absolute best. Tolkien-level, even. <br /><br />Jordan's writing sometimes frustrated me though - especially the way his characters interacted. Jordan also sometimes let his love of detail get in the way of plot development. While these were not unforgivable flaws, they could at times make the books hard to fully enjoy.<br /><br />Sanderson has effectively solved these problems. I don't know how he does it, because the book still reads like Jordan wrote it, but it is markedly better than anything the series has produced since at least books 4 and 5. I literally could not put The Gathering Storm down, which is not something I could say about the last few books in the series.<br /><br />It is as if a new Director has taken over a film or TV series that I love. The world, story, and characters remain the same, but the dialogue is delivered in a different way, and the camera angles are subtly changed to make the film flow better. Sanderson has tinkered with the details, but kept the overall story the same Wheel of Time we all love and the series is so much more enjoyable because of it.<br /><br />As far as the actual plot goes, this book essentially belongs to Egwene and Rand. We get to see both of them at their lowest before eventually coming out of the other side. This is probably the darkest this series has ever been - Rand is genuinely frightening and out of control. But the ending offers hope that, perhaps, the world can come together and defeat the Dark One after all. The Last Battle is finally here.<br /><br />Highly, highly recommended.<br /><br />** Re-read March 2020 **<br /><br />This book was both better and worse on a reread. On the one hand, I could tell the difference between Jordan and Sanderson's writing much more clearly. And like I said in my original review, most of the changes that Sanderson makes are really good! <br /><br />The plot certainly is moving much faster now, and Last Battle is tangibly close. Both Egwene and Rand's separate stories of redemption are amazing, and oh man the Seanchan battle for the White Tower was awe-inspiring. <br /><br />But I just can't quite forgive Sanderson for what he does to Mat's character. I don't want to languish on the point, because I know Sanderson is aware of it (and he makes a valiant effort to improve Mat in the next two books), but it is what it is - and for me personally some of the enjoyment of the book was ruined because Mat wasn't....Mat. <br /><br />Overall, though, this is still a great Fantasy read, and highly recommended! </span>
  <a data-text-id="4051541236681355495" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SzK0IFsrRwA8pjpo4QDPDDzO/aU25M8Yj6xyrmNe+gOsnRcnn7DuU45HzCAoz4hNdllu0UhqSgH69HzFVEbm7w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8dzqFelC6u0xRcZKPs5xXhZHB/JrKp9vdg8sZx4+2AsWc0kSLdlDvoOkMAL3ATYfXNCUhhWkGnYDVyIMKSbE5w==')})
  }
//]]>

Taking place between Oathbringer and Rhythm of War, this tale (like Edgedanc<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText10294746018454741175\" style=\"display:none\">From Brandon Sanderson—author of the #1 New York Times bestselling Stormlight Archive and its fourth massive installment, Rhythm of War—comes a new hefty novella, Dawnshard. Taking place between Oathbringer and Rhythm of War, this tale (like Edgedancer before it) gives often-overshadowed characters their own chance to shine.\n\nWhen a ghost ship is discovered, its crew presumed dead after trying to reach the storm-shrouded island Akinah, Navani Kholin must send an expedition to make sure the island hasn\'t fallen into enemy hands. Knights Radiant who fly too near find their Stormlight suddenly drained, so the voyage must be by sea.\n\nShipowner Rysn Ftori lost the use of her legs but gained the companionship of Chiri-Chiri, a Stormlight-ingesting winged larkin, a species once thought extinct. Now Rysn\'s pet is ill, and any hope for Chiri-Chiri’s recovery can be found only at the ancestral home of the larkin: Akinah. With the help of Lopen, the formerly one-armed Windrunner, Rysn must accept Navani\'s quest and sail into the perilous storm from which no one has returned alive. If the crew cannot uncover the secrets of the hidden island city before the wrath of its ancient guardians falls upon them, the fate of Roshar and the entire Cosmere hangs in the balance.<\/span>\n       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/6252.Robert_Jordan">About Robert Jordan</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/6252.Robert_Jordan"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1538507642p3/6252.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/6252.Robert_Jordan">Robert Jordan
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
11,435
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8648085730320686988"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br/><br/>Robert Jordan was the pen name of James Oliver Rigney, Jr., under which he was best known as the author of the bestselling The Wheel of Time fantasy series. He also wrote under the names <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/108933.Reagan_O_Neal' rel='nofollow noopener'>Reagan O'Neal</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/943931.Jackson_O_Reilly' title='Jackson O'Reilly' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jackson O'Reilly</a>.<br/><br/>Jordan was born in Charleston, South Carolina. He served two tours in Vietnam (from 1968 to</span>
  <span id="freeText8648085730320686988" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br /><br />Robert Jordan was the pen name of James Oliver Rigney, Jr., under which he was best known as the author of the bestselling The Wheel of Time fantasy series. He also wrote under the names <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/108933.Reagan_O_Neal" rel="nofollow noopener">Reagan O'Neal</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/943931.Jackson_O_Reilly" title="Jackson O'Reilly" rel="nofollow noopener">Jackson O'Reilly</a>.<br /><br />Jordan was born in Charleston, South Carolina. He served two tours in Vietnam (from 1968 to 1970) with the United States Army as a helicopter gunner. He was awarded the Distinguished Flying Cross with bronze oak leaf cluster, the Bronze Star with "V" and bronze oak leaf cluster, and two Vietnamese Gallantry Crosses with palm. After returning from Vietnam he attended The Citadel where he received an undergraduate degree in physics. After graduating he was employed by the United States Navy as a nuclear engineer. He began writing in 1977. He was a history buff and enjoyed hunting, fishing, sailing, poker, chess, pool, and pipe collecting. <br /><br />He described himself as a "High Church" Episcopalian and received communion more than once a week. He lived with his wife Harriet McDougal, who works as a book editor (currently with Tor Books; she was also Jordan's editor) in a house built in 1797. <br /><br />Responding to queries on the similarity of some of the concepts in his Wheel of Time books with Freemasonry concepts, Jordan admitted that he was a Freemason. However, "like his father and grandfather," he preferred not to advertise, possibly because of the negative propaganda against Freemasonry. In his own words, "no man in this country should feel in danger because of his beliefs."<br /><br />On March 23, 2006, Jordan disclosed in a statement that he had been diagnosed with cardiac amyloidosis, and that with treatment, his median life expectancy was four years, though he said he intended to beat the statistics. He later posted on his Dragonmount blog to encourage his fans not to worry about him and that he intended to have a long and fully creative life.<br /><br />He began chemotherapy treatment at Mayo Clinic in Rochester, Minnesota, in early April 2006. Jordan was enrolled in a study using the drug Revlimid just approved for multiple myeloma but not yet tested on primary amyloidosis.<br /><br />Jordan died at approximately 2:45 p.m. EDT on September 16, 2007, and a funeral service was held for him on Wednesday, September 19, 2007. Jordan was cremated and his ashes buried in the churchyard of St. James Church in Goose Creek, outside Charleston. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8648085730320686988" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
